                    </a></div></div></div><div class="table-full-width-wrap"><div class="table-wrap table-wide standard-table"><div class="table-wrap-title" id="mss278-T1" data-id="mss278-T1"><span class="label title-label" id="label-42603">Table 1.</span><div class="caption caption-id-" id="caption-42603"><p class="chapter-para">Selection of Demographic Models.</p></div> </div><div class="table-overflow"><table role="table" aria-labelledby="
                        label-42603" aria-describedby="
                        caption-42603"><thead><tr><th>Model<span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-TF1"></span><a href="javascript:;" reveal-id="mss278-TF1" data-open="mss278-TF1" class="link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn"><sup>a</sup></a><span aria-hidden="true" style="display: none;">
            . </span></th><th>Ln <em>L</em><span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-TF2"></span><a href="javascript:;" reveal-id="mss278-TF2" data-open="mss278-TF2" class="link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn"><sup>b</sup></a><span aria-hidden="true" style="display: none;">
            . </span></th><th>No. of Free<span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-TF3"></span><a href="javascript:;" reveal-id="mss278-TF3" data-open="mss278-TF3" class="link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn"><sup>c</sup></a> Parameters<span aria-hidden="true" style="display: none;">
            . </span></th><th>AIC<span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-TF4"></span><a href="javascript:;" reveal-id="mss278-TF4" data-open="mss278-TF4" class="link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn"><sup>d</sup></a><span aria-hidden="true" style="display: none;">
            . </span></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Exponential growth</td><td>−156.67</td><td>2</td><td>317.34</td></tr><tr><td>2 Epoch</td><td>−168.96</td><td>2</td><td>341.92</td></tr><tr><td>Bottleneck + growth</td><td>−156.67</td><td>3</td><td>319.34</td></tr><tr><td>3 Epoch</td><td>−168.97</td><td>4</td><td>345.94</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="table-modal"><table><thead><tr><th>Model<span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-TF1"></span><a href="javascript:;" reveal-id="mss278-TF1" data-open="mss278-TF1" class="link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn"><sup>a</sup></a><span aria-hidden="true" style="display: none;">
            . </span></th><th>Ln <em>L</em><span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-TF2"></span><a href="javascript:;" reveal-id="mss278-TF2" data-open="mss278-TF2" class="link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn"><sup>b</sup></a><span aria-hidden="true" style="display: none;">
            . </span></th><th>No. of Free<span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-TF3"></span><a href="javascript:;" reveal-id="mss278-TF3" data-open="mss278-TF3" class="link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn"><sup>c</sup></a> Parameters<span aria-hidden="true" style="display: none;">
            . </span></th><th>AIC<span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-TF4"></span><a href="javascript:;" reveal-id="mss278-TF4" data-open="mss278-TF4" class="link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn"><sup>d</sup></a><span aria-hidden="true" style="display: none;">
            . </span></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Exponential growth</td><td>−156.67</td><td>2</td><td>317.34</td></tr><tr><td>2 Epoch</td><td>−168.96</td><td>2</td><td>341.92</td></tr><tr><td>Bottleneck + growth</td><td>−156.67</td><td>3</td><td>319.34</td></tr><tr><td>3 Epoch</td><td>−168.97</td><td>4</td><td>345.94</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="table-wrap-foot"><span id="fn-mss278-TF1"></span><div content-id="mss278-TF1" class="footnote"><span class="fn"><p class="chapter-para"><sup>a</sup>The logarithm of the maximum likelihood (Ln) for each of the demographic models fit to the data.</p></span></div><span id="fn-mss278-TF2"></span><div content-id="mss278-TF2" class="footnote"><span class="fn"><p class="chapter-para"><sup>b</sup>The models assessed were exponential growth or decay (exponential growth), 2 epoch (constant and instantaneous increase), a bottleneck in the past, combined with exponential growth (bottleneck + growth), and 3 epoch (bottleneck, followed by an instantaneous increase).</p></span></div><span id="fn-mss278-TF3"></span><div content-id="mss278-TF3" class="footnote"><span class="fn"><p class="chapter-para"><sup>c</sup>The number of parameters for each model.</p></span></div><span id="fn-mss278-TF4"></span><div content-id="mss278-TF4" class="footnote"><span class="fn"><p class="chapter-para"><sup>d</sup>Akaike Information criteria [AIC = 2 × (no. free parameters) – 2 ln). The model with the minimum AIC (exponential growth) was selected as the model that best explains the data.</p></span></div></div><div class="
                        graphic-wrap
                        "><a class="fig-view-orig at-tableViewLarge openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large" target="_blank" href="/web/20231227200024/https://academic.oup.com/view-large/90601090">
                        Open in new tab
                    </a></div></div></div><p class="chapter-para">The expected SFS of variation is not affected by linkage, but that is not true of the variance (<span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-B14"></span><a href="javascript:;" reveal-id="mss278-B14" data-open="mss278-B14" class="link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr">Bustamante et al. 2001</a>; <span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-B85"></span><a href="javascript:;" reveal-id="mss278-B85" data-open="mss278-B85" class="link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr">Zhu and Bustamante 2005</a>). It is germane therefore to demonstrate that <em>S. mutans</em>, being a naturally transformable bacterial species, undergoes significant homologous gene exchange. We assessed the magnitude of recombination in <em>S. mutans</em> by identifying the number of significant gene conversion events among isolates using Sawyer’s algorithm (<span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-B70"></span><a href="javascript:;" reveal-id="mss278-B70" data-open="mss278-B70" class="link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr">Sawyer 1989</a>). This algorithm is conservative (<span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-B70"></span><a href="javascript:;" reveal-id="mss278-B70" data-open="mss278-B70" class="link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr">Sawyer 1989</a>) and therefore we regard it as an estimate of the minimum set of gene conversion events. Power analyses of the method have concluded that it tends to underestimate the gene conversion events for scenarios in which the rate of gene conversion is high (<span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-B59"></span><a href="javascript:;" reveal-id="mss278-B59" data-open="mss278-B59" class="link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr">Mansai and Innan 2010</a>). Our analysis indicates that there has been extensive gene exchange between lineages represented by the isolates in our sample (<span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-F2"></span><a href="javascript:;" data-modal-source-id="mss278-F2" class="link xref-fig">fig. 2</a><em>a</em>), with a wide distribution of gene conversion tract lengths. Additionally, our analysis with ClonalFrame suggests that on average, recombination contributes approximately six times more than mutation to the genetic variation in <em>S. mutans</em> (<em>ρ/θ</em> ≈ 6; 95% credibility interval ∼3.09–19.6; <span class="link link-data-supplement" data-supplement-target="sup1"></span><span class="content-section supplementary-material"><a path-from-xml="sup1" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20231227200024/https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mbe/30/4/10.1093_molbev_mss278/2/mss278_Supplementary_Data.zip?Expires=1706094324&amp;Signature=q-9ypMXmrfAJvE7V-MZQLJO7ttAzgHJVHCfNvAE0rveR6hLlwftoPuK37ahtH2E4E69KobbC4YiXfS6os4UTS8iLUw38AxP4uTMYpYy1ZvC3IkVkoXVVnovPRUo3i-wW0E5urFieRvtQK4xgAiYZxvzscXmjqOnYQzBRC3eRJDXyNHKHTcEfgwFPDBr6soxfiCin1EOnR~8W1PtgYwlCylIeaQRa2O-ZFVEJfZit54njdUewITLJyVfFNYO~AV4yMsUpq2jtG0oHLmcLF1~vTcxloS307J0UhPUX~d9BQf3KWV716Ra6AEIKrn3RvrJAbnaHTQhvM4MRkVcsbl-Ehg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA">supplementary fig. S8</a></span>, <span class="link link-data-supplement" data-supplement-target="sup1"></span><span class="content-section supplementary-material"><a path-from-xml="sup1" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20231227200024/https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mbe/30/4/10.1093_molbev_mss278/2/mss278_Supplementary_Data.zip?Expires=1706094324&amp;Signature=q-9ypMXmrfAJvE7V-MZQLJO7ttAzgHJVHCfNvAE0rveR6hLlwftoPuK37ahtH2E4E69KobbC4YiXfS6os4UTS8iLUw38AxP4uTMYpYy1ZvC3IkVkoXVVnovPRUo3i-wW0E5urFieRvtQK4xgAiYZxvzscXmjqOnYQzBRC3eRJDXyNHKHTcEfgwFPDBr6soxfiCin1EOnR~8W1PtgYwlCylIeaQRa2O-ZFVEJfZit54njdUewITLJyVfFNYO~AV4yMsUpq2jtG0oHLmcLF1~vTcxloS307J0UhPUX~d9BQf3KWV716Ra6AEIKrn3RvrJAbnaHTQhvM4MRkVcsbl-Ehg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA">Supplementary Material</a></span> online). We performed simulations in ms (<span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-B44"></span><a href="javascript:;" reveal-id="mss278-B44" data-open="mss278-B44" class="link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr">Hudson 2002</a>) assuming gene conversion rates similar to those estimated for <em>S. mutans</em> (six times larger than the mutation rate), all under the same demographic scenario estimated from the original data. The mean SFS over 600 simulations is similar to the observed SFS (<span class="link link-data-supplement" data-supplement-target="sup1"></span><span class="content-section supplementary-material"><a path-from-xml="sup1" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20231227200024/https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mbe/30/4/10.1093_molbev_mss278/2/mss278_Supplementary_Data.zip?Expires=1706094324&amp;Signature=q-9ypMXmrfAJvE7V-MZQLJO7ttAzgHJVHCfNvAE0rveR6hLlwftoPuK37ahtH2E4E69KobbC4YiXfS6os4UTS8iLUw38AxP4uTMYpYy1ZvC3IkVkoXVVnovPRUo3i-wW0E5urFieRvtQK4xgAiYZxvzscXmjqOnYQzBRC3eRJDXyNHKHTcEfgwFPDBr6soxfiCin1EOnR~8W1PtgYwlCylIeaQRa2O-ZFVEJfZit54njdUewITLJyVfFNYO~AV4yMsUpq2jtG0oHLmcLF1~vTcxloS307J0UhPUX~d9BQf3KWV716Ra6AEIKrn3RvrJAbnaHTQhvM4MRkVcsbl-Ehg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA">supplementary fig. S9</a></span>, <span class="link link-data-supplement" data-supplement-target="sup1"></span><span class="content-section supplementary-material"><a path-from-xml="sup1" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20231227200024/https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mbe/30/4/10.1093_molbev_mss278/2/mss278_Supplementary_Data.zip?Expires=1706094324&amp;Signature=q-9ypMXmrfAJvE7V-MZQLJO7ttAzgHJVHCfNvAE0rveR6hLlwftoPuK37ahtH2E4E69KobbC4YiXfS6os4UTS8iLUw38AxP4uTMYpYy1ZvC3IkVkoXVVnovPRUo3i-wW0E5urFieRvtQK4xgAiYZxvzscXmjqOnYQzBRC3eRJDXyNHKHTcEfgwFPDBr6soxfiCin1EOnR~8W1PtgYwlCylIeaQRa2O-ZFVEJfZit54njdUewITLJyVfFNYO~AV4yMsUpq2jtG0oHLmcLF1~vTcxloS307J0UhPUX~d9BQf3KWV716Ra6AEIKrn3RvrJAbnaHTQhvM4MRkVcsbl-Ehg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA">Supplementary Material</a></span> online). We then used the simulations to investigate the demographic inferences performed with <em>δ</em>a<em>δ</em>i. For each simulation, we estimated the SFS and inferred maximum likelihood parameters (<em>τ</em> and <em>ν</em>) for a demographic scenario of population expansion in <em>δ</em>a<em>δ</em>i. The distribution of maximum likelihood estimates of <em>τ</em> and <em>ν</em> present more variability than that obtained with classical bootstrap (<em>τ</em>: 95% CI = 0.2–2.3; <em>ν</em>: 95% CI = 2.5–11.3), and our maximum likelihood estimated parameters (<em>τ</em> = 0.355 and <em>ν</em> = 5.09) fall within the CIs obtained from the parametric bootstrap, suggesting that <em>δ</em>a<em>δ</em>i is producing results that are consistent with what would be observed in a 2 Mb chromosome evolving under such a scenario (<span class="link link-data-supplement" data-supplement-target="sup1"></span><span class="content-section supplementary-material"><a path-from-xml="sup1" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20231227200024/https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mbe/30/4/10.1093_molbev_mss278/2/mss278_Supplementary_Data.zip?Expires=1706094324&amp;Signature=q-9ypMXmrfAJvE7V-MZQLJO7ttAzgHJVHCfNvAE0rveR6hLlwftoPuK37ahtH2E4E69KobbC4YiXfS6os4UTS8iLUw38AxP4uTMYpYy1ZvC3IkVkoXVVnovPRUo3i-wW0E5urFieRvtQK4xgAiYZxvzscXmjqOnYQzBRC3eRJDXyNHKHTcEfgwFPDBr6soxfiCin1EOnR~8W1PtgYwlCylIeaQRa2O-ZFVEJfZit54njdUewITLJyVfFNYO~AV4yMsUpq2jtG0oHLmcLF1~vTcxloS307J0UhPUX~d9BQf3KWV716Ra6AEIKrn3RvrJAbnaHTQhvM4MRkVcsbl-Ehg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA">supplementary fig. S10</a></span>, <span class="link link-data-supplement" data-supplement-target="sup1"></span><span class="content-section supplementary-material"><a path-from-xml="sup1" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20231227200024/https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mbe/30/4/10.1093_molbev_mss278/2/mss278_Supplementary_Data.zip?Expires=1706094324&amp;Signature=q-9ypMXmrfAJvE7V-MZQLJO7ttAzgHJVHCfNvAE0rveR6hLlwftoPuK37ahtH2E4E69KobbC4YiXfS6os4UTS8iLUw38AxP4uTMYpYy1ZvC3IkVkoXVVnovPRUo3i-wW0E5urFieRvtQK4xgAiYZxvzscXmjqOnYQzBRC3eRJDXyNHKHTcEfgwFPDBr6soxfiCin1EOnR~8W1PtgYwlCylIeaQRa2O-ZFVEJfZit54njdUewITLJyVfFNYO~AV4yMsUpq2jtG0oHLmcLF1~vTcxloS307J0UhPUX~d9BQf3KWV716Ra6AEIKrn3RvrJAbnaHTQhvM4MRkVcsbl-Ehg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA">Supplementary Material</a></span> online). Furthermore, in our simulations, the patterns of decay of linkage disequilibrium with distance approximately resemble the decay pattern observed in the data. </p>                    <a id="90601092" scrollto-destination="90601092"></a>
<div data-id="mss278-f2" data-content-id="mss278-f2" class="fig fig-section js-fig-section" swap-content-for-modal="true"><div class="label fig-label">F<span class="small-caps">ig</span>. 2.</div><div class="graphic-wrap"><img class="content-image" src="http://web.archive.org/web/20231227200024im_/https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mbe/30/4/10.1093_molbev_mss278/2/m_mss278f2p.jpeg?Expires=1706094324&amp;Signature=Z9-UZCRnowVKEZshtFo1pZLRXlaWZwvns1oyhHO4RA0HZjaDZna5ga7ayDycSGiNw58nrtUBKt8ktBgf2QirocLwXZ7cnkTEAVWAuChNPpoHUqKJYTtTr2UHYO55FWTO5P5TJUyQvoqIgHLC7KhJ4CfvyAd8Z8C~ANaWKpOutxKMZLuY7EhsR2DtHrxvYVJNpCbSRfzDAozy9NOEGSl-Wfu3aILSzVq5FTdWaS195svFNfd~UxtAAVK1LAqWlXVSQBmdPOW6iu2miKMo9ObLe5073-bmv3folyGqtVjFvckXJ5nREoSVIS4RNFgoGOnDNmlelAv2fA~Xg4BXDgASsQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA" alt="Recombination in Streptococcus mutans. (a) The inferred distribution of recombination tracts (gene conversion) among isolates of S. mutans. Gene tracts of the core genome that served as alignment for the estimation of recombination along the genome are represented in blue and red. Tracts of significant gene conversion events detected along the genome are represented in green. (b) The distribution of gene conversion tract lengths, characterized by a wide range of values that follow a geometric distribution." data-path-from-xml="mss278f2p.jpeg"/><div class="fig-orig original-slide"><a class="fig-view-orig js-view-large at-figureViewLarge openInAnotherWindow" href="/web/20231227200024/https://academic.oup.com/view-large/figure/90601092/mss278f2p.jpeg" data-path-from-xml="mss278f2p.jpeg" target="_blank">Open in new tab</a><a data-section="90601092" href="/web/20231227200024/https://academic.oup.com/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mbe/30/4/10.1093_molbev_mss278/2/mss278f2p.jpeg?Expires=1706094324&amp;Signature=p0HIdNhstY~AKztzbyyVGeKDwJBoaM508klXJzyBpyQXaox4C1Y5cRECcsoGRH5OAwSC7Eirc-UbG7Qa~7vueH-M2~YR7t3IwJvQwNZmeoCk2cvmMh5BZmWgVpPeJxJxrkVYaEetSUOOEM8sUb9MgdbVtKoBHyZS5nulqjMo4uXMxnoPTHKgSH-0BHnPNLe6386094fiEfXMWzPqP7pntYzYPc0oO0NDO6eyhvDU2AIF74e2gPIcysPEaY0XLTCylQGAaSDR01OSWf68gbnBUstqBcHx6WqSjiSGqJ~Nymcujk8jUkJFCnYebbJVo76IUTae2fPc49KhobsS2IBcgA__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&amp;sec=90601092&amp;ar=1068944&amp;xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&amp;imagename=&amp;siteId=5325" class="download-slide" data-path-from-xml="mss278f2p.jpeg">Download slide</a></div></div><div class="caption fig-caption"><p class="chapter-para">Recombination in <em>Streptococcus mutans</em>. (<em>a</em>) The inferred distribution of recombination tracts (gene conversion) among isolates of <em>S. mutans</em>. Gene tracts of the core genome that served as alignment for the estimation of recombination along the genome are represented in blue and red. Tracts of significant gene conversion events detected along the genome are represented in green. (<em>b</em>) The distribution of gene conversion tract lengths, characterized by a wide range of values that follow a geometric distribution.</p></div></div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination="90601093" id="90601093" class="section-title js-splitscreen-section-title">Adaptation to the Postagriculture Habitat</h3>
<p class="chapter-para">To understand the role of natural selection in shaping genomic variation in <em>S. mutans</em>, we explored a variety of selection models under a similar maximum likelihood framework to that employed for the demographic fitting, used to explain the SFS of the replacement SNPs. Our analysis suggests that the majority of the changes (70%) that cause amino acid substitutions are under strong negative selection, and the remainder evolved neutrally (<span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-F3"></span><a href="javascript:;" data-modal-source-id="mss278-F3" class="link xref-fig">fig. 3</a>). The frequency of rare variants is much higher, and the frequency of common variants much lower, than expected under a neutral model, even after correcting for demographic expansion. This is a pattern consistent with strong purifying selection acting genome-wide (<span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-B14"></span><a href="javascript:;" reveal-id="mss278-B14" data-open="mss278-B14" class="link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr">Bustamante et al. 2001</a>; <span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-B10"></span><a href="javascript:;" reveal-id="mss278-B10" data-open="mss278-B10" class="link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr">Boyko et al. 2008</a>), and is in agreement with what has been observed in other bacterial species (<span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-B45"></span><a href="javascript:;" reveal-id="mss278-B45" data-open="mss278-B45" class="link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr">Hughes 2005</a>). </p>                    <a id="90601095" scrollto-destination="90601095"></a>
<div data-id="mss278-f3" data-content-id="mss278-f3" class="fig fig-section js-fig-section" swap-content-for-modal="true"><div class="label fig-label">F<span class="small-caps">ig</span>. 3.</div><div class="graphic-wrap"><img class="content-image" src="http://web.archive.org/web/20231227200024im_/https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mbe/30/4/10.1093_molbev_mss278/2/m_mss278f3p.jpeg?Expires=1706094324&amp;Signature=dtfFT3s30SEDYyTWcJIDSd1ZAeCYq4BWHpV1-n3ygosRIS~v4Fx1Mscnz0yumm3XA2pQgt2GTIYSpQK278MbMrVwe4Htjzkom7JrMTYocJbu9pKkisAEp5VFub5YUmdtQ9eW-73N38JDq53dgEQf-anLxBS2J~3ODMtbEP3Wvh6OH3b~h79hkQSdYrLA6N66-v56RTCAz671EyTuEWh3VE0Xcpmus4NgdBLtR6am0ne-LXTWpLh0MupjHRRiqygsFMUrTxbY0XJ7YF8fcq0P1lSNklwfTS--GsOtIYibsfybWb6rBvrk9dk1JsXrU2wKPDasmll~bcuBnLr3MEV-dA__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA" alt="Evidence of genome-wide selective constraints in Streptococcus mutans. The observed distribution of number of replacement SNPs at a given frequency in the sample of 58 isolates is shown in red. The expectation is that replacement changes will have an effect on the fitness of individuals, so it is unlikely that they behave neutrally. Correcting for population expansion inferred from the silent SNPs (fig. 1), does not account for the excess of singletons observed in the data (light green). On the other hand, a model that allows for selection affecting changes in allele frequency, after correcting for demography, yields a superior fit, suggesting that in the S. mutans genome 30% of the replacement changes are neutral and 70% are under strong selection (γ = −17, where γ = 2Nes, and Ne is the current population size and s is the coefficient of selection)." data-path-from-xml="mss278f3p.jpeg"/><div class="fig-orig original-slide"><a class="fig-view-orig js-view-large at-figureViewLarge openInAnotherWindow" href="/web/20231227200024/https://academic.oup.com/view-large/figure/90601095/mss278f3p.jpeg" data-path-from-xml="mss278f3p.jpeg" target="_blank">Open in new tab</a><a data-section="90601095" href="/web/20231227200024/https://academic.oup.com/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mbe/30/4/10.1093_molbev_mss278/2/mss278f3p.jpeg?Expires=1706094324&amp;Signature=zVPDd9uCDfwY6KNAm963PrrEBnF5u1rHTk0~GmYK4YHAzcm~lH-R14jm-H5slXmapdIEU0gD1om2nCLkQ8PeRPzLPgJHIWojfbYf8g8JHUOQDAWWM02AKlxHnAUIqip2k06I4wOJpdM-qomJbRfImGFz7ZHcyGp-ynfSEba-qACq~o4aCKMVguPfD5mVRlTFYyex12aH8JH-efCLkKwIRo4fUpyahIvk6XCVonrLLPJ4u3~VEKMIu-Nff09aogw1BPj3f0coyEHOSnxw3I3Fv5SD~F8CMQNzLQ6IS9MpgMNUSCJjU42tTixvXrhbEvjjKUSoQAQHuYaZ7O8atv6F2Q__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&amp;sec=90601095&amp;ar=1068944&amp;xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&amp;imagename=&amp;siteId=5325" class="download-slide" data-path-from-xml="mss278f3p.jpeg">Download slide</a></div></div><div class="caption fig-caption"><p class="chapter-para">Evidence of genome-wide selective constraints in <em>Streptococcus mutans</em>. The observed distribution of number of replacement SNPs at a given frequency in the sample of 58 isolates is shown in red. The expectation is that replacement changes will have an effect on the fitness of individuals, so it is unlikely that they behave neutrally. Correcting for population expansion inferred from the silent SNPs (<span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-F1"></span><a href="javascript:;" data-modal-source-id="mss278-F1" class="link xref-fig">fig. 1</a>), does not account for the excess of singletons observed in the data (light green). On the other hand, a model that allows for selection affecting changes in allele frequency, after correcting for demography, yields a superior fit, suggesting that in the <em>S. mutans</em> genome 30% of the replacement changes are neutral and 70% are under strong selection (<em>γ</em> = −17, where <em>γ</em> = 2<em>N</em><sub>e</sub><em>s</em>, and <em>N</em><sub>e</sub> is the current population size and <em>s</em> is the coefficient of selection).</p></div></div><p class="chapter-para">We explored the molecular adaptation of individual genes of <em>S. mutans</em> in two ways: 1) by performing neutrality tests comparing the odds ratio of replacement to silent divergent versus polymorphic changes via McDonald–Kreitman (MK) tests, and a Bayesian generalization of the Log-linear model that is the basis for the MK test (SNIPER); and 2) by identifying the protein domains, as well as the putative metabolic pathways in which these proteins are involved, of the genes present in all isolates of <em>S. mutans</em>, but not present in the outgroup <em>S. ratti</em> and two other closely related species of the mutans group (namely <em>S. macacae</em> and <em>S. criceti</em>). In particular, we were looking for proteins involved in aciduricity (resistance to acid), sugar metabolism, resistance to oxidative stress, antibiotics, and adherence to human tissue. The annotated genes of <em>S. ratti</em> were compared with the 59 <em>S. mutans</em> genomes using all versus all BLAST and from the protein clusters we identified the orthologous genes present in both species. A total of 2,033 genes were annotated in <em>S. ratti</em> and of these, 1,282 genes were in a 1:1 relationship with <em>S. mutans</em>. On average, we estimated the divergence between <em>S. mutans</em> and <em>S. ratti</em> to be approximately 26%. We estimated very few of these proteins showing signatures of positive selection (more fixed replacement changes than synonymous). The combined estimate of MK and SNIPER tests identified 14 genes that were under selection (after Bonferroni correction), the majority of which are involved in either sugar metabolism or acid tolerance (<span class="link link-data-supplement" data-supplement-target="sup1"></span><span class="content-section supplementary-material"><a path-from-xml="sup1" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20231227200024/https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mbe/30/4/10.1093_molbev_mss278/2/mss278_Supplementary_Data.zip?Expires=1706094324&amp;Signature=q-9ypMXmrfAJvE7V-MZQLJO7ttAzgHJVHCfNvAE0rveR6hLlwftoPuK37ahtH2E4E69KobbC4YiXfS6os4UTS8iLUw38AxP4uTMYpYy1ZvC3IkVkoXVVnovPRUo3i-wW0E5urFieRvtQK4xgAiYZxvzscXmjqOnYQzBRC3eRJDXyNHKHTcEfgwFPDBr6soxfiCin1EOnR~8W1PtgYwlCylIeaQRa2O-ZFVEJfZit54njdUewITLJyVfFNYO~AV4yMsUpq2jtG0oHLmcLF1~vTcxloS307J0UhPUX~d9BQf3KWV716Ra6AEIKrn3RvrJAbnaHTQhvM4MRkVcsbl-Ehg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA">supplementary table S1</a></span>, <span class="link link-data-supplement" data-supplement-target="sup1"></span><span class="content-section supplementary-material"><a path-from-xml="sup1" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20231227200024/https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mbe/30/4/10.1093_molbev_mss278/2/mss278_Supplementary_Data.zip?Expires=1706094324&amp;Signature=q-9ypMXmrfAJvE7V-MZQLJO7ttAzgHJVHCfNvAE0rveR6hLlwftoPuK37ahtH2E4E69KobbC4YiXfS6os4UTS8iLUw38AxP4uTMYpYy1ZvC3IkVkoXVVnovPRUo3i-wW0E5urFieRvtQK4xgAiYZxvzscXmjqOnYQzBRC3eRJDXyNHKHTcEfgwFPDBr6soxfiCin1EOnR~8W1PtgYwlCylIeaQRa2O-ZFVEJfZit54njdUewITLJyVfFNYO~AV4yMsUpq2jtG0oHLmcLF1~vTcxloS307J0UhPUX~d9BQf3KWV716Ra6AEIKrn3RvrJAbnaHTQhvM4MRkVcsbl-Ehg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA">Supplementary Material</a></span> online). It is possible that the relatively high divergence between <em>S. mutans</em> and <em>S. ratti</em> reduced the power of these tests, as multiple hits could mask the signature of selection; however, our results are nonetheless consistent with the SFS-based analysis.</p><p class="chapter-para">On the other hand, the analysis of proteins present in all isolates of <em>S. mutans</em>, but absent in their close relatives (the <em>S. mutans</em> unique core genome) suggests that most of these genes are involved in adaptation to the postagriculture human mouth niche. Of the 1,490 genes that conform to the core genome of <em>S. mutans</em>, 148 are present in <em>S. mutans</em> and absent in the putative sister group <em>S. ratti</em> (<span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-B78"></span><a href="javascript:;" reveal-id="mss278-B78" data-open="mss278-B78" class="link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr">Tapp et al. 2003</a>; <span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-B46"></span><a href="javascript:;" reveal-id="mss278-B46" data-open="mss278-B46" class="link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr">Hung et al. 2005</a>), whereas 73 loci are unique to <em>S. mutans</em> in comparisons involving the three species, <em>S. ratti</em>, <em>S. macacae</em><em>,</em> and <em>S. criceti</em> (<span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-F4"></span><a href="javascript:;" data-modal-source-id="mss278-F4" class="link xref-fig">fig. 4</a><em>a</em> and <span class="link link-data-supplement" data-supplement-target="sup1"></span><span class="content-section supplementary-material"><a path-from-xml="sup1" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20231227200024/https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mbe/30/4/10.1093_molbev_mss278/2/mss278_Supplementary_Data.zip?Expires=1706094324&amp;Signature=q-9ypMXmrfAJvE7V-MZQLJO7ttAzgHJVHCfNvAE0rveR6hLlwftoPuK37ahtH2E4E69KobbC4YiXfS6os4UTS8iLUw38AxP4uTMYpYy1ZvC3IkVkoXVVnovPRUo3i-wW0E5urFieRvtQK4xgAiYZxvzscXmjqOnYQzBRC3eRJDXyNHKHTcEfgwFPDBr6soxfiCin1EOnR~8W1PtgYwlCylIeaQRa2O-ZFVEJfZit54njdUewITLJyVfFNYO~AV4yMsUpq2jtG0oHLmcLF1~vTcxloS307J0UhPUX~d9BQf3KWV716Ra6AEIKrn3RvrJAbnaHTQhvM4MRkVcsbl-Ehg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA">supplementary table S2</a></span>, <span class="link link-data-supplement" data-supplement-target="sup1"></span><span class="content-section supplementary-material"><a path-from-xml="sup1" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20231227200024/https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mbe/30/4/10.1093_molbev_mss278/2/mss278_Supplementary_Data.zip?Expires=1706094324&amp;Signature=q-9ypMXmrfAJvE7V-MZQLJO7ttAzgHJVHCfNvAE0rveR6hLlwftoPuK37ahtH2E4E69KobbC4YiXfS6os4UTS8iLUw38AxP4uTMYpYy1ZvC3IkVkoXVVnovPRUo3i-wW0E5urFieRvtQK4xgAiYZxvzscXmjqOnYQzBRC3eRJDXyNHKHTcEfgwFPDBr6soxfiCin1EOnR~8W1PtgYwlCylIeaQRa2O-ZFVEJfZit54njdUewITLJyVfFNYO~AV4yMsUpq2jtG0oHLmcLF1~vTcxloS307J0UhPUX~d9BQf3KWV716Ra6AEIKrn3RvrJAbnaHTQhvM4MRkVcsbl-Ehg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA">Supplementary Material</a></span> online). Within this set of <em>S. mutans</em> unique core genes, 36 are hypothetical proteins with no similarity to known domains or protein clusters (<span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-F4"></span><a href="javascript:;" data-modal-source-id="mss278-F4" class="link xref-fig">fig. 4</a><em>a</em>). The remaining proteins show similarity with domains of proteins involved in processes of carbohydrate metabolism, resistance to acidic environments, transcriptional regulation, oxidative stress, metal and peptide translocation, and adhesion to host tissue (<span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-F4"></span><a href="javascript:;" data-modal-source-id="mss278-F4" class="link xref-fig">fig. 4</a><em>a</em> and <span class="link link-data-supplement" data-supplement-target="sup1"></span><span class="content-section supplementary-material"><a path-from-xml="sup1" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20231227200024/https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mbe/30/4/10.1093_molbev_mss278/2/mss278_Supplementary_Data.zip?Expires=1706094324&amp;Signature=q-9ypMXmrfAJvE7V-MZQLJO7ttAzgHJVHCfNvAE0rveR6hLlwftoPuK37ahtH2E4E69KobbC4YiXfS6os4UTS8iLUw38AxP4uTMYpYy1ZvC3IkVkoXVVnovPRUo3i-wW0E5urFieRvtQK4xgAiYZxvzscXmjqOnYQzBRC3eRJDXyNHKHTcEfgwFPDBr6soxfiCin1EOnR~8W1PtgYwlCylIeaQRa2O-ZFVEJfZit54njdUewITLJyVfFNYO~AV4yMsUpq2jtG0oHLmcLF1~vTcxloS307J0UhPUX~d9BQf3KWV716Ra6AEIKrn3RvrJAbnaHTQhvM4MRkVcsbl-Ehg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA">supplementary tables S2</a></span> and <span class="link link-data-supplement" data-supplement-target="sup1"></span><span class="content-section supplementary-material"><a path-from-xml="sup1" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20231227200024/https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mbe/30/4/10.1093_molbev_mss278/2/mss278_Supplementary_Data.zip?Expires=1706094324&amp;Signature=q-9ypMXmrfAJvE7V-MZQLJO7ttAzgHJVHCfNvAE0rveR6hLlwftoPuK37ahtH2E4E69KobbC4YiXfS6os4UTS8iLUw38AxP4uTMYpYy1ZvC3IkVkoXVVnovPRUo3i-wW0E5urFieRvtQK4xgAiYZxvzscXmjqOnYQzBRC3eRJDXyNHKHTcEfgwFPDBr6soxfiCin1EOnR~8W1PtgYwlCylIeaQRa2O-ZFVEJfZit54njdUewITLJyVfFNYO~AV4yMsUpq2jtG0oHLmcLF1~vTcxloS307J0UhPUX~d9BQf3KWV716Ra6AEIKrn3RvrJAbnaHTQhvM4MRkVcsbl-Ehg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA">Supplementary Data</a></span>, <span class="link link-data-supplement" data-supplement-target="sup1"></span><span class="content-section supplementary-material"><a path-from-xml="sup1" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20231227200024/https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mbe/30/4/10.1093_molbev_mss278/2/mss278_Supplementary_Data.zip?Expires=1706094324&amp;Signature=q-9ypMXmrfAJvE7V-MZQLJO7ttAzgHJVHCfNvAE0rveR6hLlwftoPuK37ahtH2E4E69KobbC4YiXfS6os4UTS8iLUw38AxP4uTMYpYy1ZvC3IkVkoXVVnovPRUo3i-wW0E5urFieRvtQK4xgAiYZxvzscXmjqOnYQzBRC3eRJDXyNHKHTcEfgwFPDBr6soxfiCin1EOnR~8W1PtgYwlCylIeaQRa2O-ZFVEJfZit54njdUewITLJyVfFNYO~AV4yMsUpq2jtG0oHLmcLF1~vTcxloS307J0UhPUX~d9BQf3KWV716Ra6AEIKrn3RvrJAbnaHTQhvM4MRkVcsbl-Ehg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA">Supplementary Material</a></span> online). In addition, some of these unique core genes contain domains potentially involved in resistance to antimicrobials, suggesting they could be of more recent acquisition (<span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-F4"></span><a href="javascript:;" data-modal-source-id="mss278-F4" class="link xref-fig">fig. 4</a><em>a</em>). Undoubtedly, one of the major challenges that <em>S. mutans</em> had to overcome as the carbohydrate content of the human diet increased was surviving at low pH. Although <em>S. mutans</em> does not constitute a significant proportion of the oral flora colonizing healthy dentition, it can become numerically significant when there is repeated and sustained acidification of the biofilms associated with excess dietary carbohydrates or impaired salivary function (<span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-B13"></span><a href="javascript:;" reveal-id="mss278-B13" data-open="mss278-B13" class="link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr">Burne 1998</a>). Interestingly, 14% of the gene products found in the <em>S. mutans</em> unique core genome have been shown to be upregulated in transcriptomic analyses at low pH (<span class="xrefLink" id="jumplink-mss278-B37"></span><a href="javascript:;" reveal-id="mss278-B37" data-open="mss278-B37" class="link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr">Gong et al. 2009</a>) (binomial test comparison with core genome, <em>P</em> = 0.01). Among these are cation flux pumps that contribute to ionic equilibrium. Analysis of the functional groups (GO terms) of the dispensable genes present in 54, 55, 56, and 57 isolates suggest that there is no enrichment of any particular functional group (<em>P</em> value &gt; 0.05 for all comparisons), when compared with the core genome and none of the genes presented mean ratio of replacement to synonymous changes (<em>k</em><sub>N</sub>/<em>k</em><sub>S</sub>) larger than 1. </p>                    <a id="90601098" scrollto-destination="90601098"></a>
<div data-id="mss278-f4" data-content-id="mss278-f4" class="fig fig-section js-fig-section" swap-content-for-modal="true"><div class="label fig-label">F<span class="small-caps">ig</span>. 4.</div><div class="graphic-wrap"><img class="content-image" src="http://web.archive.org/web/20231227200024im_/https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mbe/30/4/10.1093_molbev_mss278/2/m_mss278f4p.jpeg?Expires=1706094324&amp;Signature=QjB4hA2jPmRQZtMCVYSkjaiJLuJVGRv9IiFdVU3Rpu-qjb0JAoHpWyiA7dQzmupLDX1wUjTWU92GeOTRcNiO383wH1zkoPehvM8Vw5o9xbXAASkmZLRMVqochb08dPnH5tu0nXoO8vlqgUySgRt9S~NbX3gasdVFK4qeSWL4zv0l3wCCewsm3a1U6jjNkOFn7xCNUJZPMr4~cxlT64sp2s3F8emVMTpuHEclOYYXdWMK1YgqeN9MNfDx7UhoB6bhTXCogOaPG276f6gipmKAfqYft~zSLPWn~h6XMkzc6zgI0uWyg3-viAAZeKkHh6xnNJ3bd5kVS-gi1eMyMa1x9A__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA" alt="Genome map of Streptococcus mutans.
